</div>

</div>

Python can serve as a [scripting language](/wiki/Scripting_language "Scripting language") for [web applications](/wiki/Web_application "Web application"), e.g., via [mod_wsgi](/wiki/Mod_wsgi "Mod wsgi") for the [Apache web server](/wiki/Apache_web_server "Apache web server").<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-35_184-0" class="reference">[[184]](#cite_note-AutoNT-35-184)</sup> With [Web Server Gateway Interface](/wiki/Web_Server_Gateway_Interface "Web Server Gateway Interface"), a standard API has evolved to facilitate these applications. [Web frameworks](/wiki/Web_framework "Web framework") like [Django](/wiki/Django_(web_framework) "Django (web framework)"), [Pylons](/wiki/Pylons_(web_framework) "Pylons (web framework)"), [Pyramid](/wiki/Pyramid_(web_framework) "Pyramid (web framework)"), [TurboGears](/wiki/TurboGears "TurboGears"), [web2py](/wiki/Web2py "Web2py"), [Tornado](/wiki/Tornado_(web_server) "Tornado (web server)"), [Flask](/wiki/Flask_(web_framework) "Flask (web framework)"), [Bottle](/wiki/Bottle_(web_framework) "Bottle (web framework)") and [Zope](/wiki/Zope "Zope") support developers in the design and maintenance of complex applications. Pyjs and [IronPython](/wiki/IronPython "IronPython") can be used to develop the client-side of Ajax-based applications. [SQLAlchemy](/wiki/SQLAlchemy "SQLAlchemy") can be used as a [data mapper](/wiki/Data_mapper_pattern "Data mapper pattern") to a relational database. [Twisted](/wiki/Twisted_(software) "Twisted (software)") is a framework to program communications between computers, and is used (for example) by [Dropbox](/wiki/Dropbox_(service) "Dropbox (service)").

Libraries such as [NumPy](/wiki/NumPy "NumPy"), [SciPy](/wiki/SciPy "SciPy") and [Matplotlib](/wiki/Matplotlib "Matplotlib") allow the effective use of Python in scientific computing,<sup id="cite_ref-cise_185-0" class="reference">[[185]](#cite_note-cise-185)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-millman_186-0" class="reference">[[186]](#cite_note-millman-186)</sup> with specialized libraries such as [Biopython](/wiki/Biopython "Biopython") and [Astropy](/wiki/Astropy "Astropy") providing domain-specific functionality. [SageMath](/wiki/SageMath "SageMath") is a [computer algebra system](/wiki/Computer_algebra_system "Computer algebra system") with a [notebook interface](/wiki/Notebook_interface "Notebook interface") programmable in Python: its library covers many aspects of [mathematics](/wiki/Mathematics "Mathematics"), including [algebra](/wiki/Algebra "Algebra"), [combinatorics](/wiki/Combinatorics "Combinatorics"), [numerical mathematics](/wiki/Numerical_mathematics "Numerical mathematics"), [number theory](/wiki/Number_theory "Number theory"), and [calculus](/wiki/Calculus "Calculus").<sup id="cite_ref-ICSE_187-0" class="reference">[[187]](#cite_note-ICSE-187)</sup> [OpenCV](/wiki/OpenCV "OpenCV") has Python bindings with a rich set of features for [computer vision](/wiki/Computer_vision "Computer vision") and [image processing](/wiki/Digital_image_processing "Digital image processing").<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference">[[188]](#cite_note-188)</sup>

Python is commonly used in [artificial intelligence](/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") projects and machine learning projects with the help of libraries like [TensorFlow](/wiki/TensorFlow "TensorFlow"), [Keras](/wiki/Keras "Keras"), [Pytorch](/wiki/PyTorch "PyTorch") and [Scikit-learn](/wiki/Scikit-learn "Scikit-learn").<sup id="cite_ref-whitepaper2015_189-0" class="reference">[[189]](#cite_note-whitepaper2015-189)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference">[[190]](#cite_note-190)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference">[[191]](#cite_note-191)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference">[[192]](#cite_note-192)</sup> As a scripting language with [modular architecture](/wiki/Modular_programming "Modular programming"), simple syntax and rich text processing tools, Python is often used for [natural language processing](/wiki/Natural_language_processing "Natural language processing").<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-47_193-0" class="reference">[[193]](#cite_note-AutoNT-47-193)</sup>

Python can also be used to create games, with libraries such as [Pygame](/wiki/Pygame "Pygame"), which can make 2D games.

Python has been successfully embedded in many software products as a scripting language, including in [finite element method](/wiki/Finite_element_method "Finite element method") software such as [Abaqus](/wiki/Abaqus "Abaqus"), 3D parametric modeler like [FreeCAD](/wiki/FreeCAD "FreeCAD"), 3D animation packages such as [3ds Max](/wiki/3ds_Max "3ds Max"), [Blender](/wiki/Blender_(software) "Blender (software)"), [Cinema 4D](/wiki/Cinema_4D "Cinema 4D"), [Lightwave](/wiki/Lightwave "Lightwave"), [Houdini](/wiki/Houdini_(software) "Houdini (software)"), [Maya](/wiki/Maya_(software) "Maya (software)"), [modo](/wiki/Modo_(software) "Modo (software)"), [MotionBuilder](/wiki/MotionBuilder "MotionBuilder"), [Softimage](/wiki/Autodesk_Softimage "Autodesk Softimage"), the visual effects compositor [Nuke](/wiki/Nuke_(software) "Nuke (software)"), 2D imaging programs like [GIMP](/wiki/GIMP "GIMP"),<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference">[[194]](#cite_note-194)</sup> [Inkscape](/wiki/Inkscape "Inkscape"), [Scribus](/wiki/Scribus "Scribus") and [Paint Shop Pro](/wiki/Paint_Shop_Pro "Paint Shop Pro"),<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-38_195-0" class="reference">[[195]](#cite_note-AutoNT-38-195)</sup> and [musical notation](/wiki/Musical_notation "Musical notation") programs like [scorewriter](/wiki/Scorewriter "Scorewriter") and [capella](/wiki/Capella_(notation_program) "Capella (notation program)"). [GNU Debugger](/wiki/GNU_Debugger "GNU Debugger") uses Python as a [pretty printer](/wiki/Prettyprint "Prettyprint") to show complex structures such as C++ containers. [Esri](/wiki/Esri "Esri") promotes Python as the best choice for writing scripts in [ArcGIS](/wiki/ArcGIS "ArcGIS").<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-39_196-0" class="reference">[[196]](#cite_note-AutoNT-39-196)</sup> It has also been used in several video games,<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-40_197-0" class="reference">[[197]](#cite_note-AutoNT-40-197)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-41_198-0" class="reference">[[198]](#cite_note-AutoNT-41-198)</sup> and has been adopted as first of the three available [programming languages](/wiki/Programming_language "Programming language") in [Google App Engine](/wiki/Google_App_Engine "Google App Engine"), the other two being [Java](/wiki/Java_(software_platform) "Java (software platform)") and [Go](/wiki/Go_(programming_language) "Go (programming language)").<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-42_199-0" class="reference">[[199]](#cite_note-AutoNT-42-199)</sup>

Many operating systems include Python as a standard component. It ships with most [Linux distributions](/wiki/Linux_distribution "Linux distribution"),<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference">[[200]](#cite_note-200)</sup> [AmigaOS 4](/wiki/AmigaOS_4 "AmigaOS 4") (using Python 2.7), [FreeBSD](/wiki/FreeBSD "FreeBSD") (as a package), [NetBSD](/wiki/NetBSD "NetBSD"), [OpenBSD](/wiki/OpenBSD "OpenBSD") (as a package) and [macOS](/wiki/MacOS "MacOS") and can be used from the command line (terminal). Many Linux distributions use installers written in Python: [Ubuntu](/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system) "Ubuntu (operating system)") uses the [Ubiquity](/wiki/Ubiquity_(software) "Ubiquity (software)") installer, while [Red Hat Linux](/wiki/Red_Hat_Linux "Red Hat Linux") and [Fedora Linux](/wiki/Fedora_Linux "Fedora Linux") use the [Anaconda](/wiki/Anaconda_(installer) "Anaconda (installer)") installer. [Gentoo Linux](/wiki/Gentoo_Linux "Gentoo Linux") uses Python in its [package management system](/wiki/Package_management_system "Package management system"), [Portage](/wiki/Portage_(software) "Portage (software)").

Python is used extensively in the [information security](/wiki/Information_security "Information security") industry, including in exploit development.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-49_201-0" class="reference">[[201]](#cite_note-AutoNT-49-201)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-50_202-0" class="reference">[[202]](#cite_note-AutoNT-50-202)</sup>

Most of the [Sugar](/wiki/Sugar_(software) "Sugar (software)") software for the [One Laptop per Child](/wiki/One_Laptop_per_Child "One Laptop per Child") XO, now developed at [Sugar Labs](/wiki/Sugar_Labs "Sugar Labs"), is written in Python.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-51_203-0" class="reference">[[203]](#cite_note-AutoNT-51-203)</sup> The [Raspberry Pi](/wiki/Raspberry_Pi "Raspberry Pi") [single-board computer](/wiki/Single-board_computer "Single-board computer") project has adopted Python as its main user-programming language.

[LibreOffice](/wiki/LibreOffice "LibreOffice") includes Python, and intends to replace Java with Python. Its Python Scripting Provider is a core feature<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference">[[204]](#cite_note-204)</sup> since Version 4.0 from 7 February 2013.

## <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages_influenced_by_Python">Languages influenced by Python</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span>[edit](/w/index.php?title=Python_(programming_language)&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Languages influenced by Python")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span>

Python's design and philosophy have influenced many other programming languages:

*   [Boo](/wiki/Boo_(programming_language) "Boo (programming language)") uses indentation, a similar syntax, and a similar object model.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-90_205-0" class="reference">[[205]](#cite_note-AutoNT-90-205)</sup>
*   [Cobra](/wiki/Cobra_(programming_language) "Cobra (programming language)") uses indentation and a similar syntax, and its _Acknowledgements_ document lists Python first among languages that influenced it.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-91_206-0" class="reference">[[206]](#cite_note-AutoNT-91-206)</sup>
*   [CoffeeScript](/wiki/CoffeeScript "CoffeeScript"), a programming language that cross-compiles to JavaScript, has Python-inspired syntax.
*   [ECMAScript](/wiki/ECMAScript "ECMAScript")/[JavaScript](/wiki/JavaScript "JavaScript") borrowed iterators and [generators](/wiki/Generator_(computer_science) "Generator (computer science)") from Python.<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-93_207-0" class="reference">[[207]](#cite_note-AutoNT-93-207)</sup>
*   [GDScript](/wiki/GDScript "GDScript"), a scripting language very similar to Python, built-in to the [Godot](/wiki/Godot_(game_engine) "Godot (game engine)") game engine.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference">[[208]](#cite_note-208)</sup>
*   [Go](/wiki/Go_(programming_language) "Go (programming language)") is designed for the "speed of working in a dynamic language like Python"<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-94_209-0" class="reference">[[209]](#cite_note-AutoNT-94-209)</sup> and shares the same syntax for slicing arrays.
*   [Groovy](/wiki/Groovy_(programming_language) "Groovy (programming language)") was motivated by the desire to bring the Python design philosophy to [Java](/wiki/Java_(programming_language) "Java (programming language)").<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-95_210-0" class="reference">[[210]](#cite_note-AutoNT-95-210)</sup>
*   [Julia](/wiki/Julia_(programming_language) "Julia (programming language)") was designed to be "as usable for general programming as Python".<sup id="cite_ref-Julia_26-1" class="reference">[[26]](#cite_note-Julia-26)</sup>
*   [Nim](/wiki/Nim_(programming_language) "Nim (programming language)") uses indentation and similar syntax.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference">[[211]](#cite_note-211)</sup>
*   [Ruby](/wiki/Ruby_(programming_language) "Ruby (programming language)")'s creator, [Yukihiro Matsumoto](/wiki/Yukihiro_Matsumoto "Yukihiro Matsumoto"), has said: "I wanted a scripting language that was more powerful than Perl, and more object-oriented than Python. That's why I decided to design my own language."<sup id="cite_ref-linuxdevcenter_212-0" class="reference">[[212]](#cite_note-linuxdevcenter-212)</sup>
*   [Swift](/wiki/Swift_(programming_language) "Swift (programming language)"), a programming language developed by Apple, has some Python-inspired syntax.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference">[[213]](#cite_note-213)</sup>

Python's development practices have also been emulated by other languages. For example, the practice of requiring a document describing the rationale for, and issues surrounding, a change to the language (in Python, a PEP) is also used in [Tcl](/wiki/Tcl "Tcl"),<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-99_214-0" class="reference">[[214]](#cite_note-AutoNT-99-214)</sup> [Erlang](/wiki/Erlang_(programming_language) "Erlang (programming language)"),<sup id="cite_ref-AutoNT-100_215-0" class="reference">[[215]](#cite_note-AutoNT-100-215)</sup> and Swift.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference">[[216]](#cite_note-216)</sup>

## <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span>[edit](/w/index.php?title=Python_(programming_language)&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: See also")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span>

62.  <span class="mw-cite-backlink">**[^](#cite_ref-Reference_counting_62-0 "Jump up")**</span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"><cite class="citation web cs1">["Extending and Embedding the Python Interpreter: Reference Counts"](https://docs.python.org/extending/extending.html#reference-counts). Docs.python.org. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20121018063230/http://docs.python.org/extending/extending.html#reference-counts) from the original on 18 October 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">5 June</span> 2020</span>. <q>Since Python makes heavy use of `malloc()` and `free()`, it needs a strategy to avoid memory leaks as well as the use of freed memory. The chosen method is called _reference counting_.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Extending+and+Embedding+the+Python+Interpreter%3A+Reference+Counts&amp;rft.pub=Docs.python.org&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fdocs.python.org%2Fextending%2Fextending.html%23reference-counts&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APython+%28programming+language%29" class="Z3988"></span></span>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 June</span> 2020</span>. <q>Nim's syntax is strongly reminiscent of Python's, as it uses indented code blocks and some of the same syntax (such as the way if/elif/then/else blocks are constructed).</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=InfoWorld&amp;rft.atitle=Nim+language+draws+from+best+of+Python%2C+Rust%2C+Go%2C+and+Lisp&amp;rft.date=2017-01-16&amp;rft.aulast=Yegulalp&amp;rft.aufirst=Serdar&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.infoworld.com%2Farticle%2F3157745%2Fapplication-development%2Fnim-language-draws-from-best-of-python-rust-go-and-lisp.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APython+%28programming+language%29" class="Z3988"></span></span>
212.  <span class="mw-cite-backlink">**[^](#cite_ref-linuxdevcenter_212-0 "Jump up")**</span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"><cite class="citation web cs1">["An Interview with the Creator of Ruby"](http://www.linuxdevcenter.com/pub/a/linux/2001/11/29/ruby.html). Linuxdevcenter.com. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20180428150410/http://www.linuxdevcenter.com/pub/a/linux/2001/11/29/ruby.html) from the original on 28 April 2018<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">3 December</span> 2012</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=An+Interview+with+the+Creator+of+Ruby&amp;rft.pub=Linuxdevcenter.com&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.linuxdevcenter.com%2Fpub%2Fa%2Flinux%2F2001%2F11%2F29%2Fruby.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APython+%28programming+language%29" class="Z3988"></span></span>
213.  <span class="mw-cite-backlink">**[^](#cite_ref-213 "Jump up")**</span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"><cite id="CITEREFLattner2014" class="citation web cs1">[Lattner, Chris](/wiki/Chris_Lattner "Chris Lattner") (3 June 2014). ["Chris Lattner's Homepage"](http://nondot.org/sabre). Chris Lattner. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20151222150510/http://nondot.org/sabre/) from the original on 22 December 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">3 June</span> 2014</span>. <q>I started work on the Swift Programming Language in July of 2010\. I implemented much of the basic language structure, with only a few people knowing of its existence. A few other (amazing) people started contributing in earnest late in 2011, and it became a major focus for the Apple Developer Tools group in July 2013 [...] drawing ideas from Objective-C, Rust, Haskell, Ruby, Python, C#, CLU, and far too many others to list.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Chris+Lattner%27s+Homepage&amp;rft.pub=Chris+Lattner&amp;rft.date=2014-06-03&amp;rft.aulast=Lattner&amp;rft.aufirst=Chris&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnondot.org%2Fsabre&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APython+%28programming+language%29" class="Z3988"></span></span>
214.  <span class="mw-cite-backlink">**[^](#cite_ref-AutoNT-99_214-0 "Jump up")**</span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974"><cite id="CITEREFKupriesFellows2000" class="citation web cs1">Kupries, Andreas; Fellows, Donal K. (14 September 2000). ["TIP #3: TIP Format"](http://www.tcl.tk/cgi-bin/tct/tip/3.html). _tcl.tk_. Tcl Developer Xchange. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20170713233954/http://tcl.tk/cgi-bin/tct/tip/3.html) from the original on 13 July 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">.
